IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CIVIL ORIGINAL JURISDICTION
TRANSFER PETITION(S)(CIVIL)  NO(S).  151/2025
MEHA RUSIA                                         PETITIONER(S)
                                VERSUS
PRIYESH GUPTA                                      RESPONDENT(S)
O R D E R
1. The  petitioner  is  physically  present  before  us  and  the
respondent is present through video conferencing.
2. Both the learned counsel for the parties submitted that IA
No.28393/2026 may be taken on record, and the matter may be
disposed  of  in  terms  of  the  Settlement  Agreement  dated
31.10.2025.
3. In tune with the said Settlement Agreement, the demand draft
of Rs.17,00,000/- has been handed over in the Court in favour
of the petitioner-wife, copy of which has been placed in the
file. It is also not in dispute that the remaining part of the
amount has already been received by her. 
4. Accordingly, by invoking our power under Article 142 of the
Constitution of India, 1950, we hereby declare that there
shall be a decree of mutual divorce between the parties, as

--- Page 8 ---
2
agreed  upon.  A  decree  of  divorce  is  to  be  drawn  up
accordingly.
5. In such view of the matter, following cases stands closed:-
S.No. Case No. Remarks
1 Complaint No.286/2021 PS Vidhan Sabha Raipur
2 Complaint 
No.MO/SP/DTA/CJ/L1516/24
PS Mahila Thana, Datia
3 RCS HM/175/2024 Family Court, Datia, M.P.
4 RCT/81/2025 District Court Datia, M.P.
5 HMA/1112/2024 Family Court, Raipur, C.G.
6. It is made clear that the settlement that has been duly
arrived at between the parties shall form a part of this
order.  Needless to state that the parties are bound by the
terms of settlement which have been arrived at, between
themselves.
7. We also make it clear that henceforth, the parties shall not
make any claim as against each other. 
8. I.A. No.28393/2026 is allowed and the Transfer Petition stands
disposed of on the aforesaid terms. 
  
  ……………………………………………………………………J.
  [M.M. SUNDRESH]
       ………………………………………………………………………J.
    [NONGMEIKAPAM KOTISWAR SINGH]
NEW DELHI;
30th JANUARY, 2026

14. It is made clear that the settlement that has been duly
arrived at between the parties shall form a part of this
order.  Needless to state that the parties are bound by the
terms of settlement which have been arrived at, between
themselves.
15. We also make it clear that henceforth, the parties shall not
make any claim as against each other. 
16. I.A. No.28393/2026 is allowed and the Transfer Petition stands
disposed of on the aforesaid terms.

TRANSFER PETITION (C) NO. 3492 OF 2025
ANITA SATSANGI            Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
ANURAG SATSANGI          Respondent(s)
O R D E R
1. The present Transfer Petition has been filed by the
petitioner  –  wife  seeking  transfer  of  the  proceedings
initiated by the respondent – husband for dissolution of
marriage under Section 13(1)(ia) of the Hindu Marriage Act,
1955, being HMA No. 1923 of 2023, titled Anurag Satsangi v.
Mrs.  Anita  Satsangi  (subject-case),  pending  before  the
Additional Principal Judge, Family Court, Faridabad (Haryana)
to the Principal Judge, Family Court, Agra (Uttar Pradesh).
2. We have heard the learned counsel appearing for the
parties. 
 
3. Having regard to the fact that the petitioner is residing
with her aged parent at Agra and is taking care of her two-
year-old  child,  and  further  considering  that  two  other
proceedings between the parties, namely, M.C.No. 2449 of 2025
1

--- Page 14 ---
pending before the Principal Judge, Family Court, Agra, and
complaint case No. 20544/2025 pending before the Civil Judge
(Junior Division), Fast Track Court No. 1, Agra, are also
pending at Agra, we are of the view that it would be in the
interests of justice to transfer the subject-case as prayed
for by the petitioner.
4. Accordingly,  the  Transfer  Petition  is  allowed.  HMA
No.1923 of 2023 pending before the Additional Principal Judge,
Family  Court,  Faridabad  (Haryana)  is  transferred  to  the
Principal Judge, Family Court, Agra (Uttar Pradesh).
 
5. However,  liberty  is  reserved  to  the  respondent  to
participate in the proceedings through video conferencing. If
such a request is made, the transferee Court shall endeavour
to facilitate the same, subject to the availability of the
requisite infrastructure.
6. The transferor Court shall forthwith transmit the entire
record of the case to the transferee Court.
7. The Registry is directed to communicate this order to the
transferor Court as well as the transferee court for necessary
compliance.
2

--- Page 15 ---
8. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed of.
  .......................J.
                                 ( R. MAHADEVAN )    
 
 .......................J.

1. Heard  Mr. Arun Adlakha, learned counsel for the
petitioner with Ms. Abhipriya,  learned counsel and

--- Page 30 ---
2
Shaurya Sahay,  learned counsel appearing on advance
notice for the State.
2. The petitioner calls in question the correctness of
the order dated 11-06-2026 in CRL.MBA No. 12723/2025
passed by the High Court of Judicature at Allahabad,
Lucknow Bench. By the said order, the High Court has
denied the benefit of bail to the petitioner. The
petitioner  has  been  in  custody  for  the  past
approximately 08 months.
3. Learned counsel for the petitioner submits that the
petitioner is an innocent and  bona fide  downstream
purchaser who acquire the said property by means of a
registered  sale  deed  dated  12.10.2017  from  one
Akashdeep  Srivastava.  Learned  counsel  submits  that
Akashdeep Srivastava has already been enlarged on bail
by order dated 29.01.2026 after undergoing about one
month  in  custody.  Learned  counsel  submits  that
continued incarceration of the petitioner is wholly
unjustified.
4. Learned counsel for the State drawing attention to
the facts of the case submits that property of the
Lucknow Development Authority have been transferred and
the  property  has  changed  multiple  hands.  Learned
counsel for the State, however, submits that as to
whether  the  petitioner  is  a  bona  fide downstream
purchaser or not is a matter, which will have to be
established.

--- Page 31 ---
3
5. Having perused the records and heard learned counsel
for  the  parties,  we  are  inclined  to  enlarge  the
petitioner on bail.
6. Accordingly, we direct that the petitioner shall be
enlarged on bail subject to the satisfaction of the
Court of Judicial Magistrate-1, CJM Court, Lucknow in
Criminal Case No.17377/2026 in connection with FIR
No.304/2025  registered  at  Police  Station  Bijnor,
District  Lucknow,  Uttar  Pradesh,  for  the  offences
punishable under Sections 319(2), 318(2), 338, 336(2),
340(2),  61(2)  and  351(3)  of  the  Bharatiya  Nyaya
Sanhita, 2023.
7. The Special Leave Petition is disposed of in the
above terms.
8. Pending application(s), if any, shall also stand
disposed of.

IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CIVIL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CIVIL APPEAL NO. 46  OF 2022
((Arising out of SLP (C) No. 3616 of 2021)
K. KUMARAKRISHNAN BY HIS POWER AGENT 
M.P. KRISHNAMURTHY   … Appellant(s)
                                VERSUS
T. P. PADMAJA                                      … Respondent(s) 
O R D E R
Leave granted.
This appeal was filed challenging a final judgment and order
dated 18.11.2020 passed by the Madras High Court dismissing the
appeal being CMA No. 4286 of 2019 against an order passed by the
Family Court dismissing the application of the appellant for
divorce.
By order dated 05.03.2021, the parties were referred to the
Supreme Court Mediation Centre.  The parties have amicably settled
their disputes and a compromise deed has duly been executed.
We have perused the Compromise Deed.  The patently illegal
condition that the Appellant-husband will never in future see or
talk to or continue any relationship with his minor son, Master
Kaushik,  either  by  himself  or  through  his  relatives  is
unenforceable in law.  As observed by this Court in its order dated
20.09.2021, a child has a right to access to both his parents.  The
parties to a marriage cannot by mutual agreement surrender the
right of the child of access to both his parents.  The parties

--- Page 42 ---
2
might agree to surrender their own rights but not the rights of a
minor.  The rights of a minor of access to both parents is non-
negotiable and cannot be compromised.
The aforesaid condition, i.e. the first condition in the Deed
of Compromise being Annexure “A” to the application being I.A. No.
11723 of 2021 shall stand deleted.  
The appeal is disposed of in terms of the Memorandum of
compromise  dated  30.07.2021  being  Annexure  “A”  to  the  said
application, as rectified by this order by deletion of the first
condition therein which shall not be enforceable.
In view of the compromise arrangement between the parties and
considering  that  the  marriage  between  the  Appellant  and  the
Respondent has irretrievably broken down, this Court, in exercise
of its power under Article 142 of the Constitution of India, to do
complete justice between the parties, hereby passes a decree of
divorce  under  Section  13-B  of  the  Hindu  Marriage  Act,  1955
dissolving the marriage of the Appellant and the Respondent by
mutual consent.
Pending applications, if any, stand disposed of accordingly.
………………………………………………………,J.
(Indira Banerjee)
………………………………………………………,J.
(J.K. Maheshwari)
New Delhi;
January 03, 2022.

          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. The submission of the learned counsel for the
petitioner is that Office Memorandum (“O.M.”) issued by
the Ministry of Home Affairs which is in force since
23.08.1993 is to be construed as one to protect lady
I.P.S probationers and not as one which dis-entitles
them to undertake training even if they are fit to
undertake training.
2. It is the case of the petitioner that she
delivered a child on 20.09.2025 and volunteered for
the  requisite  training  which  were  to  commence  on
22.06.2026 but, because of this O.M. which provides for
a  year’s  hiatus  in  training  post  delivery,  the
Department did not permit her to undertake training.
Accordingly, the said O.M. was challenged before the
Central Administrative Tribunal (“Tribunal”) which, by
a  detailed  order,  permitted  the  petitioner  to
participate in the Phase-II training which were to
commence on 22.06.2026 subject to fulfillment of the
requisite  undertakings,  formalities,  medical
requirements,  etc.  While  passing  the  said  interim
order, the Tribunal had also noticed the submissions
made on behalf of the petitioner that earlier Ms
Anupama James and Ms Arti Singh were given exemption
2

--- Page 49 ---
from the rigors of the O.M.
3. Issue notice.
4. Notice on behalf of the respondent has been
accepted by Dr M. Vishakhamurthy, AOR.
5. As it appears from the impugned order that
training were to commence from 22.06.2026, we deem it
appropriate  to  require  the  learned  ASG  to  seek
instructions whether at this stage the petitioner can
join the training.
6. Put up on 10.07.2026.

          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. Heard  Mr.  Balbir  Singh, learned  Senior  Counsel  for  the
petitioners,  Mr.  Sudhanshu  Choudhari,  learned  Senior  Counsel
1

--- Page 99 ---
appearing for respondent No.5, on caveat, Mr. Sandeep Deshmukh,
learned AOR for respondent No.1 and Mr. Kunal Cheema, learned AOR
appearing for respondent No.7, on caveat.
2. On  the  special  facts  of  this  case  and  considering  the
peculiarities  involved, we  are not  inclined to  exercise our
jurisdiction under Article 136 of the Constitution of India. The
Special Leave Petition is dismissed.
3. At this stage, Mr. Balbir Singh, learned Senior Counsel for
the petitioners submits that the observations made in the impugned
order will come in the way of the adjudicational suits on merits.
It is needless to state that the observations are made for the
purpose  of  adjudicating  the  interim  application  and  making
consequential orders. The further proceedings in the suit would be
decided uninfluenced by the observations made in the impugned
order.
4. At this stage, Mr. Kunal Cheema, learned AOR appearing for
respondent No.7, on caveat, submits that the appeal against order
filed by his client namely Appeal From Order (ST) No.21361/2025 is
still pending. Learned counsel submits that there are independent
points to be argued. It is needless to state that as and when the
appeal is taken up, the parties may place their submissions on
those independent points and the High Court may pass appropriate
orders in accordance with law.
5. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed of.
  (NEHA GUPTA)                                  (MANOJ KUMAR)
COURT MASTER (SH)                             COURT MASTER (NSH)

1. By judgment dated 11.12.2024 passed by the Judicial
Magistrate No.2, Bharatpur (Rajasthan) in Criminal Complaint
Case No.163 of 2024, the petitioner was convicted for the
offence under Section 138 of the Negotiable Instruments Act,
1881 and sentenced to undergo simple imprisonment for two
years and directed to pay compensation of Rs. 9,50,000/-, in
default  whereof,  to  undergo  simple  imprisonment  for  a
further  period  of  six  months.  Aggrieved  thereby,  the
petitioner preferred Criminal Appeal No. 5 of 2025 before
1

--- Page 181 ---
the Additional Sessions Judge No. 4, Bharatpur (Rajasthan),
which came to be dismissed by judgment dated 29.11.2025.
Thereafter, the petitioner filed Criminal Revision Petition
No. 149 of 2026 before the High Court of Judicature for
Rajasthan Bench at Jaipur, along with Application No. 24 of
2026 seeking suspension of sentence. By the impugned order
dated  19.05.2026,  the  High  Court  dismissed  the  said
application. Hence, the present Special Leave Petition.
2. After  arguing  the  matter  for  some  time,  learned
counsel for the petitioner submits that in support of the
prayer for suspension of sentence, the petitioner is willing
to deposit the compensation amount of Rs.9,50,000/- (Rupees
Nine Lakhs and Fifty Thousand only) by way of a Demand Draft
in favour of the Registrar, Supreme Court of India, New
Delhi. For this purpose, he seeks one week’s time.
3. Acceding to the said request, list the matter after
one week.

Pursuant to our order dated 27.05.2026, respondent no.4 -
Dr. Nikhil Tandon, the Acting Director of All India Institute of

--- Page 185 ---
2
Medical Sciences (hereinafter referred to as the “AIIMS”) is
personally present in Court. Though this Court had directed him to
be personally present along with his explanation today, a reply
affidavit on his behalf has been filed. The Court takes a strong
view to such conduct also. When an explanation was asked for, he
has only filed a reply affidavit.
2. Dr. Tandon has personally explained his position and has
tendered unconditional apology for the conduct of the authorities
of AIIMS. 
3. Even coming to the reply affidavit filed by him, we find that
on the one hand he has tendered apology but in the same breath,
some justification has also been given in the said reply affidavit
for committing such contemptuous act which was clearly in the teeth
of the order of this Court.
4. At this stage, Ms. Aishwarya Bhati, learned ASG prays for
indulgence and submits that she may be permitted to withdraw the
said reply affidavit and file a fresh explanation.
5. Having regard to the aforesaid, by way of extra-ordinary
indulgence, the matters be listed on 09.07.2026 at 12:30 p.m.
6. As respondent no.4 has personally tendered unconditional and
unqualified apology before the Court, his personal appearance
stands dispensed with, for the present.
